  - [18:45:51 - 18:47:03] **Blind Trust and Automation Bias**

    (Amanda Lim): Hi Prof, I'm not able to put up my hand either. I just typed it in the comment box. I feel like there's also the potential of police officers just blindly trusting these algorithms and losing the ability to do some independent judgment.

    (Professor): Okay, so there is a concern that police officers may over-rely on the algorithm. There is a tendency to simply adopt what a machine tells you—a bias towards following the machine. If they just blindly trust the machine, they may act in a way that disregards their own personal experience, their own training, and their own instincts. This may actually lead to worse policing indeed.

    (Amanda Lim)：教授好，我也无法举手。我刚刚在评论框里打字了。我觉得还有一个风险是，警官可能会盲目信任这些算法，从而丧失进行独立判断的能力。

    (教授)：好的，所以有人担心警官可能会过度依赖算法。人们往往倾向于直接采纳机器的建议——这是一种追随机器的偏见。如果他们只是盲目信任机器，可能会在行动中忽视自己的个人经验、训练和直觉。这实际上可能会导致警务工作质量下降。

  - [18:47:03 - 18:49:14] **Methodological Flaws and Blind Spots**

    (Chan Meow Ling Jacqelene): I'm talking more about the methodology here. If there is an error rate, I think one of the risks would be leading the police to investigate non-crimes and actually miss the actual crimes involved. Because the AI profiling uses algorithms, if there is an overgeneralization or an error rate, it doesn't really explain that correlation does not mean causation. It will lead to an error where the police think a certain group of people are more likely to be involved. So, it would lead them to investigate those people who are non-criminals, and actually miss out on opportunities to detect the actual crimes.

    (Professor): So I suppose the use of these algorithms may potentially lead to blind spots, because perhaps the algorithm doesn't capture all aspects of reality. It will lead to certain crimes being under-policed and certain crimes being over-policed. Is that what you are referring to?

    (Chan Meow Ling Jacqelene): Yes, that's what I'm trying to say.

    (Professor): Yeah, so that is a methodological question regarding the accuracy and scope of these systems.

    (Chan Meow Ling Jacqelene)：我更多是想谈谈方法论的问题。如果存在错误率，我认为风险之一是会导致警方去调查非犯罪行为，而实际上错过了真正的犯罪。因为人工智能侧写使用的是算法，如果存在过度概括或错误率，它并不能真正解释相关性不代表因果性。这会导致一种错误，即警方认为某类人群更有可能涉案。因此，这会导致他们去调查那些非罪犯的人，从而错失侦破实际犯罪的机会。

    (教授)：所以我认为使用这些算法可能会导致盲点，因为算法可能无法捕捉到现实的所有方面。这将导致某些犯罪监管不足，而某些犯罪监管过度。你是这个意思吗？

    (教授)：是的，这正是我想表达的。

    (教授)：对，所以这是一个关于这些系统的准确性和范围的方法论问题。

  - [18:49:14 - 18:50:48] **Misuse for Targeting Specific Groups**

    (Low Xuan Yin): Sorry, took me a few seconds to unmute. I think for this question, it may target certain specific groups. It can be misused by certain people to focus on certain racial, ethnic, or political groups. So instead of preventing crime fairly, maybe they can single out specific people or communities without a very good reason.

    (Professor): So the systems themselves may potentially be misused for purposes other than actually lowering the total crime rate. There is a possibility that certain police forces will instead use these systems to target certain groups of people in an unfair way. The problem with this kind of misuse is that it can be quite difficult to prove, because all that is happening is a shift of police resources and strategy. It may be difficult to actually identify that such targeting is going on.

    (Low Xuan Yin)：抱歉，我花了几秒钟才解除静音。我认为关于这个问题，它可能会针对特定的群体。它可能被某些人滥用，专门针对特定的种族、民族或政治团体。因此，与其公平地预防犯罪，他们可能会毫无理由地挑出特定的人或社区。

    (教授)：所以系统本身可能会被滥用于非降低总犯罪率的目的。某些警察部队可能会利用这些系统以不公平的方式针对特定人群。这种滥用的问题在于很难取证，因为表面上发生的只是警力资源和策略的转移。很难实际识别出这种针对性行为正在发生。

  - [18:50:48 - 18:54:31] **Accountability and Transparency Issues**

    (Kanupriya Malhotra): Another risk could be that it could undermine the accountability that the police might take. If a police decision relies only on complex AI models, it might be difficult for citizens to even question decisions. And then the responsibility essentially shifts from a human's judgment to the judgment of a system, so it becomes blurred. If any harm occurs or if there's any misclassification, is it the responsibility of the officer, the software company, or the police department as a whole?

    (Professor): Yes, the use of such systems gives rise to the question: if something goes wrong, who do you hold responsible? When it comes to the actual decision to arrest someone, it is clear the police force is responsible. But when it comes to policing strategy—shifting officers, targeting certain places or individuals in a general fashion—this kind of generalized "wrongdoing" is a bit more difficult to assign blame for. Do you blame the police force for adopting what the algorithm says, or do you blame the algorithm for unjustifiably moving resources? That is the accountability problem.

    (Lavnit): It was actually me in the chat, but my point was similar to Kanu's, just adding the lens of transparency. Since this predictive policing is done by complex machine learning algorithms, if they are not communicated to citizens, citizens may not know why they are being targeted or why the neighborhood is labeled as high-risk with more patrols. It links back to accountability and transparency.

    (Professor): There is a clear issue here. Under normal circumstances, if a police force seems to be heavily policing a particular area, you might be able to demand an explanation. But if the police force is relying on an algorithm that isn't transparent about how it works—a "black box"—then no explanation can possibly be given. All they can say is, "Oh, the algorithm says so, that's why we're doing this."

    (Kanupriya Malhotra)：另一个风险是它可能会削弱警方的问责制。如果警方的决定仅仅依赖于复杂的人工智能模型，市民可能很难质疑这些决定。责任本质上从人类的判断转移到了系统的判断，界限变得模糊。如果发生任何伤害或分类错误，是警官的责任，软件公司的责任，还是整个警察部门的责任？

    (教授)：是的，使用这类系统会引发一个问题：如果出了问题，谁来负责？在逮捕某人的具体决定上，显然是警方负责。但当涉及到警务策略——调动警员、针对特定地点或个人——这种一般性的“不当行为”就比较难归咎了。你是怪警方采纳了算法的建议，还是怪算法不合理地调动了资源？这就是问责问题。

    (Lavnit)：其实聊天框里是我，但我的观点和 Kanu 的相似，只是增加了透明度的视角。由于这种预测性警务是由复杂的机器学习算法完成的，如果不对市民公开，市民可能不知道为什么自己被针对，或者为什么他们的社区被标记为高风险区并有更多巡逻。这与问责制和透明度是紧密相关的。

    (教授)：这里显然有个问题。在正常情况下，如果警方似乎在严密管控某个区域，你也许可以要求解释。但如果警方依赖的是一个运作方式不透明的算法——一个“黑箱”——那么他们根本无法给出解释。他们只能说，“噢，算法是这么说的，所以我们就这么做。”

  - [18:54:31 - 18:56:20] **Effectiveness and Data Drift**

    (Professor): I think in the chat, Wen Yue had a point. If your microphone is working, do you want to verbalize that?

    (Tang Wen Yue): Sorry, yes. Basically, the point is that in terms of effectiveness, because AI is trained on past datasets trying to correlate certain hotspots with geographic or spatial data, if there are new crimes or different types of crime that start trending that are not within the training dataset, then predictive policing becomes less effective. This is similar to what we learned in other courses, called "data drift." There's a risk that predictive policing becomes less effective over time as criminals come up with new types of crimes, and the AI cannot react fast enough.

    (Professor): This becomes particularly problematic and is related to the blind trust problem. If a police force over-relies on AI, it may result in the police force being less proactive and less alert to different patterns of crime.

    (教授)：我想聊天框里 Wen Yue 有个观点。如果你的麦克风没问题，你想口头阐述一下吗？

    (Tang Wen Yue)：抱歉，好的。基本上，我的观点是关于有效性的。因为人工智能是根据过去的数据集进行训练的，试图将某些热点与地理或空间数据相关联。如果出现了训练数据集中没有的新犯罪或不同类型的犯罪趋势，那么预测性警务就会变得不那么有效。这类似于我们在其他课程中学到的“数据漂移”（data drift）。随着罪犯想出新的犯罪类型，人工智能无法足够快地做出反应，预测性警务的有效性会随时间降低。

    (教授)：这会变得特别成问题，并且与盲目信任的问题有关。如果警方过度依赖人工智能，可能会导致警方不再那么积极主动，对不同模式的犯罪也会降低警惕。

  - [18:56:20 - 18:57:40] **Data Vulnerability and Security**

    (Tushar Pande): I have a point to make, I also can't raise my hand. To do this kind of predictive AI for policing, there's a large bit of data that's stored, which is very personal and sensitive information. Having this kind of personally sensitive information leads to a lot of cybersecurity or misuse of information issues—let's say by rogue police officers. So that brings that element of concern.

    (Professor): I guess when you rely on algorithms that rely on data, and you have to collect a considerable amount of data, it gives rise to the usual vulnerabilities relating to data. This could include misuse by some rogue police officer who perhaps wants to take revenge on a particular person, or there is a risk of a third party somehow managing to get access to the data.

    (Tushar Pande)：我有个观点，我也举不了手。要做这种用于警务的预测性人工智能，需要存储大量数据，其中包含非常个人和敏感的信息。拥有这类个人敏感信息会导致许多网络安全问题或信息滥用问题——比方说被不良警官滥用。这就带来了这方面的担忧。

    (教授)：我想当你依赖于基于数据的算法，并且必须收集大量数据时，就会产生通常与数据相关的数据漏洞。这可能包括被某个想报复特定人的不良警官滥用，或者存在第三方设法获取数据的风险。

  - [18:57:40 - 19:00:10] **Gamification and Planting Evidence**

    (Benhur): Hello. Gamification of the system is always a risk.

    (Professor): What do you mean by gamification?

    (Benhur): If the wrong people or people with ill intentions get access to these systems, you can plant evidence which would point towards a particular person being profiled as high risk, just to reduce their chances of getting a visa approved, or even as revenge. Of course, I'm talking about extreme cases, but I think there's always a risk.

    (Professor): That's an interesting point. If you figure out what the "red flags" are for the algorithm, you may potentially plant those red flags on a certain place or person, creating negative consequences for them. You mentioned this might be a subset of data vulnerability, but I think the point you are trying to get at is more that you are actually feeding bad data into the system intentionally.

    (Benhur)：你好。系统的游戏化（gamification）始终是一个风险。

    (教授)：你所说的游戏化是什么意思？

    (Benhur)：如果错误的人或怀有恶意的人接触到这些系统，他们可以伪造证据，指向某个特定的人，使其被归类为高风险，目的只是为了降低他们获得签证批准的机会，甚至作为报复。当然，我说的是极端情况，但我认为这种风险始终存在。

    (教授)：这是一个有趣的观点。如果你弄清楚了算法的“危险信号”（red flags）是什么，你可能会把这些信号栽赃给某个地点或某个人，从而给他们带来负面后果。你提到这可能是数据漏洞的一个子集，但我认为你想表达的观点更多是关于故意向系统输入错误数据。

  - [19:00:10 - 19:01:37] **Presumption of Innocence**

    (Liau Yun Qing): Hi! I'm thinking, I don't know whether it works in Singapore, but basically there's something called "innocent until proven guilty." If the AI is saying "oh, you are doing something wrong," how do I even prove that I'm not? How can I defend myself? I think this is part of the transparency problem. As the person who is caught, I wouldn't be able to defend myself because I can't afford lawyers to fight an algorithm.

    (Professor): It depends on how you use the system. If the system progresses to the point where we are not only using it to allocate police resources but also to figure out whether someone actually committed a crime or the likelihood of it, then there is a concern that you are making a presumption of guilt just because the system says "most likely this person did it." This is, of course, contrary to how most legal systems operate, where someone is assumed to be innocent until the legal system proves they are guilty.

    (Liau Yun Qing)：嗨！我在想，虽然不知道在新加坡是否适用，但基本上有个原则叫“无罪推定”。如果人工智能说“噢，你在做坏事”，我该如何证明我没有？我该如何为自己辩护？我认为这是透明度问题的一部分。作为被抓的人，我无法为自己辩护，因为我请不起律师来对抗算法。

    (教授)：这取决于你如何使用系统。如果系统的发展到了我们不仅用它来分配警力资源，还用来判断某人是否实际犯罪或犯罪的可能性，那么就存在一种担忧：仅仅因为系统说“这个人最可能做了”，你就做出了有罪推定。这当然与大多数法律系统的运作方式相悖，即在法律系统证明某人有罪之前，假定其无罪。

  - [19:01:53 - 19:03:34] **Summary of Risks: Bad Data and Displacement Effect**

    If there are no other points, I do have a couple more things to highlight. One of the things the article mentions is the problem of bad data. This is a very simple problem: ultimately, some human being has to collect the data and put it into the system. There is always a chance that that human being might make a mistake. If a mistake is made, the system will reflect that data in its predictions, leading to poor predictions for the police force. One other point which might be relevant here is the so-called "displacement effect." This effect happens when the police force focuses their attention on one particular area. The goal is to reduce the amount of crime, but what could in fact happen is that the crime simply moves to a different place. The displacement effect causes a different location to suffer from a higher rate of crime, rather than actually reducing the level of crime overall.

    如果没有其他观点，我还有几点要强调。文章提到的一点是错误数据的问题。这是一个非常简单的问题：归根结底，必须有人去收集数据并将其输入系统。这就总有可能出现人为错误。如果出了错，系统将在其预测中反映该数据，导致警方的预测出现偏差。另一点可能相关的是所谓的“替代效应”（displacement effect）。当警方将注意力集中在某个特定区域时，就会发生这种效应。目标是减少犯罪数量，但实际上可能发生的是犯罪仅仅转移到了另一个地方。替代效应导致另一个地点的犯罪率上升，而不是真正降低整体犯罪水平。

  - [19:03:34 - 19:08:49] **Automated Judicial Decision-Making**

    Let's move on now to discuss a different aspect of legal automation, which is automated judicial decision-making. This is a more recent phenomenon that has become much more serious because generative AI has come into the picture. Generative AI is good at producing text, and judges also produce a lot of text, so the idea has come up that perhaps we might rely on AI to take over some or all functions of what judges do—which is to make the right judicial decisions. As a bit of background, I should mention that if you look at how judges actually operate today, to some extent, judges already work in a somewhat automated fashion. For example, lower court judges don't have a free hand to decide however they like. They are forced to apply the rules that have been adopted by a higher court judge. In this sense, their decision is sort of automated. Additionally, in the common law system, judges generally follow precedents—they decide like cases alike. Finally, and this is more current, judges have begun to create and use algorithmic frameworks of decision-making.

    Let me give you an example on the next slide. What you see here is a sentencing framework for a particular crime: the crime of distributing intimate images of another person without their consent. The courts have developed this framework to decide how to sentence someone who has committed such a crime. It is a very rule-based, algorithmic one. Step 1: The court considers the level of culpability (how blameworthy is the criminal) and harm (how much harm was done to the victim). Step 2: The court identifies the indicative sentencing range based on the sentencing matrix on the right. For example, if culpability is medium and harm is moderate, the sentencing range is 15 to 30 months of imprisonment with the option of caning. Step 3: The court determines the appropriate "starting point" within that range (e.g., 20 months). Step 4: The court applies aggravating and mitigating factors to increase or decrease the punishment. Step 5: The court applies the "totality principle" to determine whether the end result is sufficient and proportionate. This framework already sort of automates the way judges make decisions.

    现在让我们转而讨论法律自动化的另一个方面，即自动化司法决策。这是一个较新的现象，随着生成式人工智能的出现，这个问题变得更加严峻。生成式人工智能擅长生成文本，而法官也产出大量文本，因此产生了一个想法：也许我们可以依靠人工智能来接管法官的部分或全部职能——即做出正确的司法判决。作为背景，我要提一下，如果你观察法官今天的实际运作方式，在某种程度上，法官的工作已经有点自动化了。例如，下级法院的法官不能随心所欲地判决。他们被迫应用上级法院法官采用的规则。在这个意义上，他们的决定是某种程度上的自动化。此外，在普通法系中，法官通常遵循先例——同案同判。最后，也是更当前的情况，法官已经开始创建并使用算法式的决策框架。

    我在下一张幻灯片举个例子。这里展示的是针对特定犯罪——未经同意散布他人私密图像——的量刑框架。法院制定了这个框架来决定如何对此类罪犯进行量刑。这是一个非常基于规则的算法式框架。第一步：法院考虑罪责程度（罪犯有多大过错）和伤害程度（对受害者造成了多大伤害）。第二步：法院根据右侧的量刑矩阵确定指示性量刑范围。例如，如果罪责是中等，伤害是中等，量刑范围就是15到30个月监禁，并可处以鞭刑。第三步：法院在该范围内确定合适的“起刑点”（例如20个月）。第四步：法院应用加重和减轻情节来增加或减少惩罚。第五步：法院应用“总和原则”来确定最终结果是否充分且相称。这个框架在某种程度上已经自动化了法官的决策方式。

  - [19:08:49 - 19:10:15] **Non-Automated Aspects: Compassion and Empathy**

    Before I go into the ethical issues, it is useful to consider: what are aspects of judicial decision-making that are *not* automated?

    (Chan Meow Ling Jacqelene): Maybe those that involve a moral or ethical judgment that requires human empathy, like family disputes or cases where compassion is needed.

    (Professor): So things like compassion or empathy which feed into how judges come to a final decision may not be automated. You can try to build compassion into a machine, but I think you will find that quite difficult. This is distinctly a human thing. This can apply to judgments where, for example, the criminal committed a particular crime out of necessity or because they were under a lot of pressure.

    在进入伦理问题之前，思考一下这个问题很有用：司法决策中有哪些方面是*无法*自动化的？

    (Chan Meow Ling Jacqelene)：也许是那些涉及道德或伦理判断、需要人类同理心的方面，比如家庭纠纷或需要同情的案件。

    (教授)：所以像同情心或同理心这些影响法官最终裁决的因素可能无法自动化。你可以尝试将同情心植入机器，但你会发现这非常困难。这是人类特有的东西。这可能适用于这样的判决：例如，罪犯是出于必要或在巨大压力下实施了特定犯罪。

  - [19:10:15 - 19:13:23] **Translating Real World Facts and Weighing Factors**

    (Yan Fok): Hello? I think judicial decision-making involves taking into consideration mitigating factors like the context. For example, you could have an accident and hurt someone, but did you stop to help or run away? Or a person's past character or contributions to society. Even within the 15 to 30 months range, do I give 16 months or 30 months? A lot is up to the judge and the arguments presented. That might be a limitation to how AI can think humanly in that way.

    (Professor): You raised two things. First, an AI system *can* take into account aggravating and mitigating factors, but how does the AI system actually incorporate such factors? There needs to be a human being who can translate facts of the world and decide whether the evidence suggests that such a mitigating factor exists. This is about looking at the real world and seeing what is the case—something difficult for an AI to do. The second point is the "weighing" point. After you take into account a particular factor, you need to weigh it. How much should this aggravating factor increase the sentence? This is something a human judge will naturally do.

    (Yan Fok)：喂？我认为司法决策涉及考虑像背景这样的减轻情节。例如，你可能出了事故伤了人，但你是停下来帮忙还是逃跑了？或者一个人的过往品行或对社会的贡献。即使在15到30个月的范围内，我是判16个月还是30个月？这在很大程度上取决于法官和呈上的论据。这可能是人工智能无法像人类那样思考的局限性。

    (教授)：你提到了两点。首先，人工智能系统*确实可以*考虑加重和减轻情节，但人工智能系统实际上如何整合这些因素呢？需要有一个人将现实世界的事实“翻译”出来，并决定证据是否表明存在这样的减轻情节。这涉及到观察现实世界并判断情况——这是人工智能很难做到的。第二点是“权衡”。在考虑了特定因素后，你需要权衡它。这个加重情节应该增加多少刑期？这是人类法官自然会做的事情。

  - [19:13:23 - 19:15:04] **Physical Observations and Credibility Assessment**

    (Lavnit): My point is fairly similar, but more about physical observations in the courtroom. This is something I don't think AI can take note of. Example: whether the defendant showed some remorse in the courtroom. Also, assessing the credibility of witnesses or alibis. Only a human judge can do that based on whoever is presented from the prosecution and defense.

    (Professor): Maybe in the future AI can do that, but for now, only a human judge can look at a witness or defendant and assess how credible their story is—looking not only at what they are saying but *how* they are saying it, their facial expressions, and so on. That's an important part of the process of adjudication.

    (Lavnit)：我的观点很类似，但更多是关于法庭上的物理观察。我认为这是人工智能无法注意到的。例如：被告在法庭上是否表现出悔意。还有，评估证人或不在场证明的可信度。只有人类法官才能根据控辩双方的人员表现做出判断。

    (教授)：也许未来人工智能可以做到，但目前，只有人类法官可以看着证人或被告，评估他们的故事有多可信——不仅看他们说什么，还要看他们*怎么*说，他们的面部表情等等。这是裁决过程的重要组成部分。

  - [19:15:04 - 19:16:17] **Punitive Punishment and Deterrence**

    (Pang Qin Wei): I'm thinking about whether they can decide on punitive punishment, especially for the case of deterrence when the case is unique or the first of its kind. I think you can't rely on automation to decide that. For example, punitive punishment for a tech company to act as a deterrent.

    (Professor): I guess maybe you need a human being to ascertain or see how much punishment is needed in order to deter a particular thing.

    (Pang Qin Wei)：我在想它们能否决定惩罚性刑罚，特别是当案件是独特的或首例案件时的威慑作用。我认为你不能依靠自动化来决定这一点。例如，对科技公司进行惩罚性处罚以起到威慑作用。

    (教授)：我想也许你需要人类来确定或判断需要多大的惩罚力度才能对特定事物起到威慑作用。

  - [19:16:17 - 19:19:19] **Social Authority and Jury Diversity**

    (Tushar Pande): One part of legal judgment is essentially society's acceptance of the decision. This is traditionally construed by cognitive thinking, emotions, and juggling with the facts. That part is not automated through AI. The acceptance is not automated unless it's decided by a human weighing all facts. I call it social acceptance or cognitive ability.

    (Professor): I would call it "social authority." Society places its authority and trust in human judges to make decisions on its behalf. That is something which only the human judge can exercise, because a human judge is part of that society.

    (Sophie): For trials that value a jury decision, the government appreciates the life experience and diverse perspectives that a group of people bring. So when it's just based on past outcomes and data, you lose that diversity of perspective.

    (Professor): In systems that still retain the jury—a panel of laypersons who decide guilt—you can't really replace that group because they bring a diversity of life experience that AI cannot automate.

    (Tushar Pande)：法律判决的一个部分本质上是社会对决定的接受度。这传统上是由认知思维、情感和对事实的权衡构成的。这部分是通过人工智能无法自动化的。除非是由人类权衡所有事实后做出决定，否则这种接受度是无法自动化的。我称之为社会接受度或认知能力。

    (教授)：我会称之为“社会权威”。社会将其权威和信任赋予人类法官，让他们代表社会做出决定。这是只有人类法官才能行使的，因为人类法官本身就是那个社会的一部分。

    (Sophie)：对于重视陪审团裁决的审判，政府看重的是一群人带来的生活经验和多元视角。如果仅仅基于过去的结果和数据，你就失去了这种视角的这种多样性。

    (教授)：在仍然保留陪审团制度——即由一群外行决定是否有罪——的体系中，你无法真正取代那个群体，因为他们带来了人工智能无法自动化的丰富生活经验。

  - [19:19:19 - 19:21:49] **Subjectivity vs. Objectivity in Sentencing**

    (Tan Tit Ho): I was actually thinking from the sentencing framework you showed. In actual fact, even humans are very subjective. Things like "state of mind" or "intentional vs accidental" are subjective. Even the starting point within a range—should it be 17 or 19 months?—is subjective. Also, factors like age: if an aggressor is 90 years old but has a bodybuilder physique, is he treated as another frail 90-year-old? AI would not be swayed by these visual factors or subjectivity. In fact, AI could be a lot more impartial in doing the automation of the sentencing itself.

    (Professor): You raised two points. One relates to the drawing out of circumstances—a human judge will account for circumstances they can observe, rightly or wrongly. But your point about subjectivity is really a point *in favor* of using AI. Arguably, we want our decision-making to be as objective as possible to avoid biases and human subjectivity. Possibly, if you allow an AI system to make decisions, it could do so in a way which is completely objective.

    (Tan Tit Ho)：其实我是在思考你展示的那个量刑框架。事实上，即使是人类也非常主观。像“精神状态”或“故意与意外”这样的事情都是主观的。即使是范围内的起刑点——是17个月还是19个月？——也是主观的。还有像年龄这样的因素：如果侵害者是90岁但拥有健美运动员的体格，他会被当作另一个虚弱的90岁老人对待吗？人工智能不会受到这些视觉因素或主观性的影响。事实上，人工智能在量刑自动化方面可能会更加公正。

    (教授)：你提到了两点。一点关于情境的提取——人类法官会考虑他们能观察到的情境，无论对错。但你关于主观性的观点实际上是支持使用人工智能的论据。可以说，我们希望决策尽可能客观，以避免偏见和人类的主观性。如果你让人工智能系统做决定，它可能会以一种完全客观的方式进行。

  - [19:21:49 - 19:23:01] **Discussion: Is it Ethical to Replace Judges with AI?**

    Given what we know, is it ethical for us or for any society to seek to replace a judge with an AI system? As mentioned, one argument in favor is objectivity.

    基于我们所知，对于我们或任何社会来说，寻求用人工智能系统取代法官是否符合伦理？如前所述，支持的一个论点是客观性。

  - [19:23:01 - 19:24:32] **Hidden Bias in Historical Data**

    (Zhang Xiaoyue): To follow up on the bias part, AI bias is more hidden because the algorithms are trained on data. Based on historical information, the algorithm may actually just replicate or even amplify those discriminations. It is very hard for us to identify and detect.

    (Professor): That is a good point. There is a concern that AI operates on the basis of historical data. If the historical data is biased in a certain direction—for example, if a certain minority group has historically been given heavier sentences—and you put that data into the AI system, the system is going to automatically judge any future persons in that minority group and sentence them to a heavier sentence, just because that is how it has been trained.

    (Zhang Xiaoyue)：关于偏见部分，我想补充一点，人工智能的偏见更加隐蔽，因为算法是基于数据训练的。基于历史信息，算法实际上可能只是复制甚至放大了那些歧视。我们很难识别和检测到这一点。

    (教授)：这是个好观点。人们担心人工智能是基于历史数据运作的。如果历史数据在某个方向上存在偏见——例如，某个少数群体历史上被判处了更重的刑罚——而你将这些数据输入人工智能系统，系统将自动审判该少数群体的任何未来被告，并判处更重的刑罚，仅仅因为它是这样被训练的。

  - [19:24:32 - 19:25:32] **The Problem of Novel Cases**

    (Chan Meow Ling Jacqelene): If there is a case where no similar precedent exists, AI will not be able to make a prediction or come to a reasonable outcome.

    (Professor): This is the problem of novel cases. Novel cases are a difficult problem even for human lawyers and judges, because you are trying to apply the law to something not seen before. AI systems may simply not be able to properly account for such novel cases because they don't form part of the training data.

    (Chan Meow Ling Jacqelene)：如果出现没有类似先例的案件，人工智能将无法做出预测或得出合理的结果。

    (教授)：这就是新颖案件的问题。即使对人类律师和法官来说，新颖案件也是个难题，因为你要将法律应用于前所未见的事物。人工智能系统可能根本无法妥善处理此类新颖案件，因为它们不构成训练数据的一部分。

  - [19:25:32 - 19:27:21] **The Challenge of Appeals**

    (Pang Qin Wei): I'm wondering, if AI makes decisions, how would the appeal system work? If the AI is doing all the decision-making, you don't know how it works. Can we appeal based on our own system? I'm curious how the appeal system will collapse under this system.

    (Professor): That's an interesting question. In most judicial systems, there are further courts above that you can appeal to. The idea is that you get heard by a different judge of a higher authority who can overrule the lower court. But if you have a system entirely based on AI, there seems to be no point of appeal, because you would just be appealing to the same system which will come to the exact same outcome. Perhaps there is no choice but to have a human being involved in the appeal stage.

    (Pang Qin Wei)：我在想，如果由人工智能做决定，上诉系统该如何运作？如果全由人工智能决策，你又不知道它是如何运作的。我们能基于自己的系统上诉吗？我很好奇上诉系统在这个体系下会不会崩溃。

    (教授)：这是个有趣的问题。在大多数司法系统中，上面还有你可以上诉的高级法院。其理念是你由一位更高权威的不同法官审理，他可以推翻下级法院的裁决。但如果你有一个完全基于人工智能的系统，上诉似乎就没有意义了，因为你只是向同一个系统上诉，它会得出完全相同的结果。也许在上诉阶段必须有人类参与。

  - [19:27:21 - 19:30:25] **Reasoning vs. Processing**

    (Tushar Pande): A lot of it is about reasoning. Different judges use representation of facts in different ways to put together an intelligent argument. In the case of an AI replacement, that would be universal, and we would lose that flexibility where people construe facts to come to a decision which has a societal impact. Societal impact is not a tangible thing understood by AI. My argument is that intelligent interpretation of facts to come to a logical decision is unique to a human.

    (Professor): Reasoning is a distinctly human thing. AI appears to reason, but actually, it is processing data and coming up with an output. What is lost is the human reasoning process. This takes us into legal theory: people deserve to know *why* a decision has been made. You won't be satisfied if a judge just says "Guilty, go to jail." Furthermore, without reasoning, there is nothing for you to dispute. Because judges are obliged to provide reasons, this allows for the potential for appeal.

    (Tushar Pande)：这很大程度上关乎推理。不同的法官以不同的方式陈述事实，以此构建明智的论点。如果用人工智能替代，那将是千篇一律的，我们会失去那种人们解释事实以做出具有社会影响的决定的灵活性。社会影响不是人工智能能理解的有形事物。我的论点是，对事实进行智能解读以做出逻辑决定是人类独有的。

    (教授)：推理是人类特有的东西。人工智能看起来在推理，但实际上它是在处理数据并产出结果。我们失去的是人类的推理过程。这涉及到法律理论：人们有权知道*为什么*做出某个决定。如果法官只说“有罪，去坐牢”，你是不会满意的。此外，没有推理，你就没有东西可争辩。因为法官有义务提供理由，这才使得上诉成为可能。

  - [19:30:25 - 19:32:35] **Separation of Powers and Captured Judiciary**

    (Tang Wen Yue): The point I wanted to make was that the judiciary is the third pillar of government, in addition to the legislative and executive. If AI replaces those judges, that effectively hands over one pillar of the government to whoever controls the algorithms and the AI. If we take the US as a case study, that could have severe consequences if tech billionaires are the ones controlling how the judiciary functions. Instead of a check and balance, the people have no accountability for it.

    (Professor): This is an important issue—the loss of a check in society. If the AI system is developed by the private sector, you might have a "captured judiciary," meaning a judicial system where there is a conflict of interest. If you are the person developing this AI system, you may well have an incentive to tweak it in such a way that it favors your interests.

    (Tang Wen Yue)：我想表达的观点是，司法是除立法和行政之外的政府第三支柱。如果人工智能取代了法官，那就实际上把政府的一根支柱拱手让给了控制算法和人工智能的人。如果我们以美国为例，如果科技亿万富翁控制了司法的运作方式，后果可能非常严重。不再有制衡，人民对此也无法问责。

    (教授)：这是一个重要问题——社会制衡的丧失。如果人工智能系统是由私营部门开发的，你可能会遇到“被俘获的司法”（captured judiciary），即存在利益冲突的司法系统。如果你是开发这个人工智能系统的人，你很有可能有动机对其进行调整，使其有利于你的利益。

  - [19:32:35 - 19:34:21] **Efficiency and Routine Cases**

    (Professor): Lavnit also had a different point in the chat: AI can increase the efficiency of judicial decision-making. That is definitely a plus point. Depending on the legal system, judiciaries can take a very long time to come to decisions. Efficiency is a problem. Perhaps there may be a case for AI systems to be used for simple and routine cases where the stakes are low, like traffic violations. In these types of cases, maybe you can farm out the decision-making to an AI system, with guardrails in place, such as allowing people to appeal to a human judge.

    (教授)：Lavnit 在聊天框里还有一个不同的观点：人工智能可以提高司法决策的效率。这绝对是一个加分项。取决于法律体系，司法部门可能需要很长时间才能做出决定。效率是个问题。也许有理由将人工智能系统用于风险较低的简单常规案件，比如交通违规。在这类案件中，也许你可以将决策外包给人工智能系统，并设立防护措施，例如允许人们向人类法官上诉。

  - [19:34:21 - 19:36:04] **Conclusion on Judicial Automation**

    I will round up the discussion about judicial decision-making here. If you have a judicial system that basically operates on an AI, you may lose the human aspect of judicial decision-making in terms of the loss of compassion, empathy, and perhaps more importantly, the loss of the authority of the court. If people don't trust how an AI system operates—especially because AI systems don't give reasons—then the judicial system itself loses authority over society. That is one of the ways that societies collapse. We will pause for 10 minutes and come back at 7:45 to talk about the automation of legal services.

    我将在此总结关于司法决策的讨论。如果你有一个基本依靠人工智能运作的司法系统，你可能会失去司法决策中的人性方面，包括同情心、同理心的丧失，也许更重要的是，法院权威的丧失。如果人们不信任人工智能系统的运作方式——特别是因为人工智能系统不给出理由——那么司法系统本身就会失去对社会的权威。这是社会崩溃的方式之一。我们将休息10分钟，7点45分回来讨论法律服务的自动化。

  - [19:46:01 - 19:49:37] **Automation of Legal Services**

    Great. Let's resume our seminar. We have talked about predictive policing and automated judicial decision-making. The last thing I want to mention is the automation of legal services. This is one area that has gained a lot of attention as a result of the rise of generative AI. Just like judges, lawyers work very much with words, so the theory is that generative AI could potentially be used to do things that lawyers have traditionally been doing—for example, providing legal advice, drafting documents like wills and contracts, and court advocacy (speaking to a judge in court). Just like with traditional automation, there are potential benefits to automating legal services using AI. There is an interest in increasing people's access to justice, particularly for those who may not be able to afford the services of a human lawyer. The theory is that an AI system could provide an alternative, cheaper source of legal service. Additionally, there is an interest in increasing the speed of legal services and reducing costs.

    To set some background, let's look at a couple of articles. A recent survey found that half of the people surveyed would actually trust an AI system to help them write their will. A will is a fairly important document if you have resources you want to distribute after your death, yet apparently, many people would trust AI to draft it, despite the potential risks. Another article, which you can see on the right-hand side of the screen, relates to court advocacy. This refers to an experiment—I believe done in 2023—where two individuals, instead of making their own legal arguments, simply wore a Bluetooth earpiece and repeated to the judge what an AI system told them. This was one early experiment of using AI in the context of court advocacy.

    好。让我们继续研讨会。我们已经讨论了预测性警务和自动化司法决策。我想提到的最后一点是法律服务的自动化。随着生成式人工智能的兴起，这一领域受到了极大关注。就像法官一样，律师的工作主要是与文字打交道，因此理论上，生成式人工智能可以被用来处理律师的传统工作——例如提供法律建议、起草遗嘱和合同等文件，以及法庭辩护（在法庭上对法官陈词）。与传统自动化一样，利用人工智能自动化法律服务也有潜在的好处。人们有兴趣增加诉诸司法的机会，特别是对于那些负担不起人类律师费用的人。理论上，人工智能系统可以提供一种替代的、更便宜的法律服务来源。此外，人们也希望提高法律服务的速度并降低成本。

    为了提供一些背景信息，我们来看几篇文章。最近的一项调查发现，一半的受访者实际上信任人工智能系统帮他们起草遗嘱。如果你有死后想要分配的资产，遗嘱是一份相当重要的文件，但显然，尽管存在潜在风险，许多人仍然信任人工智能来起草它。屏幕右侧的另一篇文章涉及法庭辩护。这指的是一个实验——我相信是在2023年进行的——在这个实验中，两名个人并没有自己进行法律辩论，而是戴着蓝牙耳机，向法官复述人工智能系统告诉他们的话。这是在法庭辩护背景下使用人工智能的一个早期实验。

  - [19:49:37 - 19:54:29] **Ethical Problems: Confidentiality and Inaccuracy**

    Given these examples, we can discuss two distinct problems: first, from the perspective of individual lawyers using AI; and second, from the broader societal perspective of turning towards AI for legal services. So, what are the potential ethical problems?

    (Wu Hang/Jessica): I think the most important ethical problem could be the sensitivity of the information. When a client talks to a lawyer, the lawyer needs to abide by strict attorney-client confidentiality. But when people talk to AI, they tend to trust it and give a lot of detailed, private information. The AI may use that information as public data when training its algorithms.

    (Professor): Yes, client confidentiality is definitely a concern. Lawyers take confidentiality extremely seriously; deliberately or accidentally disclosing client information can get a lawyer into a lot of trouble because it can be personally or commercially sensitive. This is a two-pronged problem. If lawyers use AI to provide services and type client data into the system, there is a chance the AI service provider will use that data to train the next AI model. That client information then forms part of the training dataset and may potentially be revealed when the new system is used. From a societal standpoint, when individuals use generative AI systems themselves to get legal advice, they input their own information, creating the same problem if the company uses it for training.

    (Low Xuan Yin): I think AI systems can make mistakes or give outdated information. Laws change very often, so if the AI was trained on old information and does not have updated data, it may provide advice based on rules that are no longer valid. It can also misunderstand a legal question or give an answer that sounds correct but is actually wrong.

    (Professor): This is the problem of legal inaccuracy, or "hallucination." Usually, the reason you go to a lawyer is that you want a professional guarantee that what they are saying is actually the law and applies to your case. When you use an AI system, there is a chance it may be outdated or simply inaccurate. If you act on the basis of that wrong advice, it may cause you potential harm.

    鉴于这些例子，我们可以讨论两个截然不同的问题：一是从律师个人使用人工智能的角度；二是从社会转向人工智能寻求法律服务的更广泛角度。那么，潜在的伦理问题有哪些？

    (Wu Hang/Jessica)：我认为最重要的伦理问题可能是信息的敏感性。当客户与律师交谈时，律师必须遵守严格的律师-客户保密义务。但是当人们与人工智能交谈时，他们往往会信任它并提供大量详细的私人信息。人工智能在训练算法时可能会将这些信息视为公共数据使用。

    (教授)：是的，客户保密绝对是一个问题。律师非常重视保密性；故意或意外泄露客户信息会给律师带来大麻烦，因为这些信息可能涉及个人隐私或商业机密。这是一个双重问题。如果律师使用人工智能提供服务并将客户数据输入系统，人工智能服务提供商可能会利用这些数据来训练下一个模型。这样客户信息就成了训练数据集的一部分，并可能在新系统使用时被泄露。从社会角度来看，当个人自己使用生成式人工智能系统获取法律建议时，他们输入了自己的信息，如果公司利用这些信息进行训练，也会产生同样的问题。

    (Low Xuan Yin)：我认为人工智能系统可能会犯错或提供过时信息。法律经常变化，如果人工智能是基于旧信息训练的，没有更新数据，它可能会基于已失效的规则提供建议。它也可能误解法律问题，或者给出一个听起来正确但实际上错误的答案。

    (教授)：这就是法律不准确或“幻觉”的问题。通常你去律师那里是因为你想要一个专业保证，确信他们所说的确实是法律并且适用于你的情况。当你使用人工智能系统时，它有可能是过时的或者是完全不准确的。如果你根据那个错误的建议行事，可能会给你带来潜在的伤害。

  - [19:54:29 - 19:56:27] **Abuse of Legal Process**

    (Liang Kaixin): I think regarding individuals using AI for legal services, there was a case in Singapore where people used it for defamation and abuse. There is a likelihood of people abusing the system because the legal fees become very low. They can just cast a case against any individual that criticized them and cause that individual to incur huge legal fees to respond.

    (Professor): That is an interesting problem: the abuse of legal process. This is where people sue not because they have a valid complaint, but because they want to trouble or threaten someone else. One issue that arises with AI is that it makes it cheaper to abuse the legal process in this way. You can ask the AI to draft your submissions—even if they are substandard—and submit them to the court. This makes it cheaper for you to sue people you don't like. That is one interesting problem generative AI can create.

    (Liang Kaixin)：我认为关于个人使用人工智能获取法律服务，新加坡有一个案例，人们利用它进行诽谤和滥用。人们很有可能滥用该系统，因为法律费用变得非常低。他们可以对任何批评他们的个人提起诉讼，导致对方不得不承担巨额法律费用来应诉。

    (教授)：这是一个有趣的问题：对法律程序的滥用。这是指人们起诉不是因为他们有合理的投诉，而是因为他们想给别人制造麻烦或威胁别人。人工智能带来的一个问题是，它降低了以这种方式滥用法律程序的成本。你可以让人工智能起草你的法律文书——即使是不合标准的——然后提交给法庭。这使得起诉你不喜欢的人变得更便宜。这是生成式人工智能可能带来的一个有趣问题。

  - [19:56:27 - 19:58:37] **Duty of Care and Unauthorized Practice**

    (Kanupriya Malhotra): One of the potential ethical problems is that the blind usage of AI by lawyers could challenge the duty of care. It is their professional responsibility to provide competent legal advice. If they set the precedent that we can use AI to make these decisions, it might encourage non-lawyers or companies to use AI tools to deliver legal services. This could result in the unauthorized practice of law, blurring the line between legal advice and legal information.

    (Professor): I guess there are two distinct problems here. The first is if lawyers use it irresponsibly—using AI to draft submissions without checking—which is a violation of the duty of care to their clients. The second is that generative AI tools designed for legal services may make it easier for unscrupulous people to practice law without authorization.

    (Kanupriya Malhotra)：潜在的伦理问题之一是，律师盲目使用人工智能可能会挑战审慎责任（duty of care）。提供胜任的法律建议是他们的职业责任。如果他们开了先例，让我们认为可以用人工智能来做这些决定，这可能会鼓励非律师人士或公司使用人工智能工具来提供法律服务。这可能导致未经授权的法律执业，模糊了法律建议和法律信息之间的界限。

    (教授)：我想这里有两个不同的问题。首先是如果律师不负责任地使用它——比如用人工智能起草文书而不加检查——这就违反了对客户的审慎责任。其次是专为法律服务设计的生成式人工智能工具可能会让无良之人更容易在未经授权的情况下从事法律执业。

  - [19:58:37 - 20:00:03] **Loss of Legal Privilege**

    (Wong Kee Fong): How about the loss of legal professional privilege? Is there a way that can be contained when using AI tools? People might willingly or unknowingly share their problems with AI tools.

    (Professor): This is definitely a concern that has recently gotten attention. The idea behind professional privilege is that when you tell your lawyer something, that information is protected from court disclosures. But people may not realize that when they ask ChatGPT for "legal advice," what they put into ChatGPT may potentially be incriminating. That information is not subject to legal professional privilege. They may be, in a sense, incriminating themselves when they ask ChatGPT legal questions. That is a potential risk people may not be aware of.

    (Wong Kee Fong)：那法律职业特权（legal professional privilege）的丧失呢？使用人工智能工具时有什么方法可以控制吗？人们可能会自愿或不知不觉地与人工智能工具分享他们的问题。

    (教授)：这绝对是最近受到关注的一个问题。职业特权的核心理念是，当你告诉律师某事时，该信息受到保护，免于向法庭披露。但人们可能没有意识到，当他们向 ChatGPT 寻求“法律建议”时，他们输入 ChatGPT 的内容可能会使自己入罪。该信息不受法律职业特权的保护。从某种意义上说，当他们向 ChatGPT 询问法律问题时，可能是在自证其罪。这是人们可能没有意识到的一个潜在风险。

  - [20:00:03 - 20:01:16] **The "Black Box" Problem**

    (Li Jiayin): There is also the problem of the "black box." Many AI systems' internal logic and decision-making processes are unknown and not explainable. When lawyers use such a system, it's very hard for them to explain the recommendation's foundation in depth, which might cause distrust between the lawyer and the customer.

    (Professor): This applies to systems that are not text-based, where the AI just comes up with a probability of guilt or innocence. If the AI system is a black box and cannot be explained, then just like in the judicial system, this can lead to distrust of legal advice.

    (Li Jiayin)：还有一个“黑箱”问题。许多人工智能系统的内部逻辑和决策过程是未知且无法解释的。当律师使用这样的系统时，他们很难深入解释推荐的基础，这可能会导致律师和客户之间的不信任。

    (教授)：这适用于那些非基于文本的系统，即人工智能只是给出一个有罪或无罪的概率。如果人工智能系统是一个无法解释的黑箱，那么就像在司法系统中一样，这会导致对法律建议的不信任。

  - [20:01:16 - 20:04:24] **De-skilling and Loss of "Lawcraft"**

    (Yan Fok): I echo the point about making abuse of process cheaper. You can use GenAI to explore multiple different scenarios of how to launch a legal attack against a target. The other point relates to budding lawyers. If they rely a lot on AI now to learn and practice law, it would deteriorate their "lawcraft." Without AI, lawyers' mental muscles are very good, but over-reliance brings down their mental finesse. If new areas of law emerge in the future—like laws for a new way of the world in 2100—and the current generation has lost that fitness, they may be less mentally equipped to come up with new laws, especially since AI won't have future data to model on.

    (Professor): This is a point I struggle with in my day-to-day job teaching law students. This is the problem of loss of ability or training. This happens if law students or young lawyers over-rely on AI tools to produce their work. You get lawyers who stop thinking for themselves and become dependent on AI systems to write their work and decide what to say in court.

    (Yan Fok)：我赞同关于滥用程序成本降低的观点。你可以利用生成式人工智能探索多种不同的方案来对目标发起法律攻击。另一点涉及新手律师。如果他们现在非常依赖人工智能来学习和实践法律，那将会退化他们的“法律技艺”（lawcraft）。没有人工智能时，律师的思维肌肉非常发达，但过度依赖会降低他们的思维细腻度。如果未来出现了新的法律领域——比如针对2100年新世界模式的法律——而这一代人已经失去了这种能力，他们可能在心理上更难以制定新法律，尤其是因为人工智能没有未来的数据可供建模。

    (教授)：这是我在教法学学生的日常工作中非常纠结的一点。这就是能力或训练丧失的问题。如果法学学生或年轻律师过度依赖人工智能工具来完成工作，就会发生这种情况。你会得到不再独立思考的律师，他们变得依赖人工智能系统来写作和决定在法庭上说什么。

  - [20:04:24 - 20:07:13] **Loss of Holistic Consideration**

    (Raphael): I guess law sometimes is quite subjective. You need to consider precedents and other cases. I'm not sure how relying on AI might lose the subjectivity aspect, but if you're not feeding it enough context, it may not be that complete. It might miss what you would have looked for or considered if you were human.

    (Professor): I would frame this as a loss of the holistic consideration of facts. Lawyers are actually supposed to try to be objective—subjectivity is not something lawyers aspire towards—but they need to holistically consider the facts of every case. For example, when a good lawyer gives advice to a client about a commercial matter, they don't just take what the client tells them and apply the law. They exercise their experience to ask further questions, bringing in all necessary facts about what the client is trying to do, what they are selling, and how the market works. This allows the lawyer to give the best possible advice. If someone relies entirely on an AI system, there may be a loss of this holistic consideration.

    (Raphael)：我想法律有时是相当主观的。你需要考虑先例和其他案件。我不确定依赖人工智能会如何失去主观性方面，但如果你没有给它足够的背景信息，它可能就不完整。它可能会错过如果你是人类会去寻找或考虑的东西。

    (教授)：我会将其重新表述为对事实的整体考量的缺失。实际上律师应该尽量客观——主观性并非律师所追求的——但他们需要整体地考量每个案件的事实。例如，当一位优秀的律师就商业事务向客户提供建议时，他们不会只是听客户说什么就直接应用法律。他们会运用经验进一步提问，引入所有关于客户意图、销售内容以及市场运作方式的必要事实。这使得律师能够提供尽可能好的建议。如果某人完全依赖人工智能系统，可能会失去这种整体考量。

  - [20:07:13 - 20:10:41] **Hallucinated Citations and Professor's View**

    (Professor): There was a point in the chat by Lavnit relating to inaccuracy and hallucination of citations. This is a distinct problem that has come up in practice: lawyers submit documents to court where the AI has produced a case that doesn't exist, or a case that exists but doesn't make the point the lawyer claims. This creates a problem because it's inaccurate and doesn't help the client. More importantly, it potentially pollutes the legal process. If the judge doesn't catch the hallucination, that citation becomes part of the judgment, and an AI hallucination becomes part of the legal system, which is pretty catastrophic.

    Someone asked for my personal take on the topic. As someone training future lawyers, what disturbs me the most is the potential loss of a lawyer's ability to think, write, and speak for themselves. It is not clear to me that AI will advance to the point where it can fully take on roles lawyers have traditionally held. If that happens, the legal system as a whole will suffer for it.

    (教授)：Lavnit 在聊天中提到了关于引用不准确和幻觉的问题。这是一个在实践中已经出现的独特问题：律师向法庭提交的文件中，人工智能生成了一个不存在的案例，或者一个存在但并不支持律师观点的案例。这制造了问题，因为它不仅不准确，也帮不了客户。更重要的是，它可能会污染法律程序。如果法官没有发现这个幻觉，该引用就会成为判决的一部分，人工智能的幻觉就成了法律体系的一部分，这是相当灾难性的。

    有人问我对这个话题的个人看法。作为一名培养未来律师的人，最让我困扰的是律师独立思考、写作和表达能力的潜在丧失。我不认为人工智能会发展到可以完全承担律师传统角色的地步。如果那种能力丧失的情况发生，整个法律体系都将为此受损。

  - [20:10:41 - 20:14:23] **Medical Automation: Context and Examples**

    Okay, we are done with legal automation, so now we can move on to medical automation. Countries have become much more interested in using AI to automate certain aspects of providing medical services. Examples include diagnosis (a patient types symptoms into an AI tool which churns out a diagnosis), automation of medical advice, treatment (administering medicine, conducting surgery), and counseling.

    In terms of development so far, a new AI tool has recently been used by surgeons for spinal surgery in Singapore, which apparently led to better outcomes. But at the same time, the middle article here highlights concerns: as we allow AI to infiltrate the medical profession, malfunctions or missed conditions can result in harm. The article mentions botched surgeries and misidentified body parts when AI is used. The last article on the right is interesting. Geoffrey Hinton, a Nobel Prize winner and AI pioneer, famously said in 2016 that we no longer need radiologists because AI systems can automatically scan images to detect tumors. However, it is now 2026, and not only have radiologists not gone extinct, but there is an increased demand for them. This suggests there may be a risk that we are overestimating what AI can actually do in the medical field.

    好，法律自动化的内容就到这里，现在我们进入医疗自动化。各国对利用人工智能自动化医疗服务的某些方面变得越来越感兴趣。例子包括诊断（患者将症状输入人工智能工具，工具给出诊断）、医疗建议自动化、治疗（给药、进行手术）以及心理咨询。

    就目前的发展而言，新加坡的外科医生最近使用了一种新的人工智能工具进行脊柱手术，据说效果更好。但与此同时，中间的文章强调了担忧：当我们允许人工智能渗透到医疗行业时，故障或漏诊可能会导致伤害。文章提到了人工智能使用时出现的手术失败和身体部位识别错误。右边的最后一篇文章很有意思。诺贝尔奖得主、人工智能先驱杰弗里·辛顿（Geoffrey Hinton）在2016年曾有一句名言，说我们不再需要放射科医生了，因为人工智能系统可以自动扫描图像检测肿瘤。然而，现在是2026年，放射科医生不仅没有灭绝，需求反而增加了。这表明我们可能高估了人工智能在医学领域的实际能力。

  - [20:14:23 - 20:16:34] **Risks: Over-dependence and System Failure**

    We can explore the ethical concerns. What ethical risks can arise if we use AI to provide medical services?

    (Bob): I think one thing is over-reliance. If people are too reliant on AI, say there is a power outage or the medical service relying on AI breaks, doctors who rely too much on it might lose the ability to do it on their own.

    (Professor): So there is an issue about over-dependence. Similar to lawyers, there is a risk that doctors may over-rely on AI systems. When the AI malfunctions or power goes out, we may have doctors unable to provide treatment or diagnosis. That is a potential risk that can cause harm to patients.

    我们可以探讨一下伦理问题。如果我们使用人工智能提供医疗服务，会出现哪些伦理风险？

    (Bob)：我认为一点是过度依赖。如果人们太依赖人工智能，比如发生停电或者依赖人工智能的医疗服务崩溃了，那些过度依赖它的医生可能会失去独立工作的能力。

    (教授)：所以存在过度依赖的问题。与律师类似，医生也有过度依赖人工智能系统的风险。当人工智能发生故障或停电时，我们可能会面临医生无法提供治疗或诊断的情况。这是一个可能对患者造成伤害的潜在风险。

  - [20:16:34 - 20:18:37] **Risks: Misdiagnosis and Information Guidance**

    (Chan Meow Ling Jacqelene): I guess one risk is the inclusion of irrelevant information or exclusion of relevant information by the AI. These errors will result in the AI generating wrong diagnosis, prognosis, and treatment plans. That's from the perspective of the patients.

    (Professor): This is the problem of misdiagnosis. Even with a perfect AI tool, misdiagnosis can happen because of over- or under-inclusion of information. This relates to whether you can substitute a clinician. Patients themselves don't always know what is relevant; they need to be guided by an experienced clinician to disclose relevant information. Sometimes patients say too much or hide things, and the doctor has to painstakingly tease out the history. If you rely on the patient to just provide information to an AI without guidance, this can result in misdiagnosis.

    (Chan Meow Ling Jacqelene)：我想一个风险是人工智能包含无关信息或排除相关信息。这些错误会导致人工智能生成错误的诊断、预后和治疗方案。这是从患者的角度来看的。

    (教授)：这就是误诊的问题。即使有一个完美的人工智能工具，误诊也可能发生，因为信息的过度包含或包含不足。这涉及到你是否可以替代临床医生的问题。患者自己并不总是知道什么是相关的；他们需要经验丰富的临床医生引导来披露相关信息。有时患者说得太多或隐瞒事情，医生必须费力地梳理病史。如果你依赖患者在没有指导的情况下仅向人工智能提供信息，这可能导致误诊。

  - [20:18:37 - 20:20:40] **Risks: De-skilling vs. Supplementation**

    (Md Ghazali Nasir): I have points regarding over-dependence. It intensifies the de-skilling of physicians. On the other hand, having AI could help gather information because AI can process more research papers than a physician would be able to read.

    (Professor): One good use case of AI is gathering information from medical research articles. AI is very good at summarizing this kind of information for the doctor. This is a valuable use case that acts as supplementation rather than replacement. But strictly, there is the point about de-skilling of doctors as well.

    (Md Ghazali Nasir)：我有关于过度依赖的观点。它加剧了医生的技能丧失。另一方面，拥有人工智能可以帮助收集信息，因为人工智能处理研究论文的能力远超医生的阅读量。

    (教授)：人工智能的一个很好的用例是从医学研究文章中收集信息。人工智能非常擅长为医生总结这类信息。这是一个有价值的用例，它起到的是补充而非替代的作用。但严格来说，这也确实存在医生技能丧失的问题。

  - [20:20:40 - 20:22:21] **Risks: Data Privacy and Breaches**

    (Low Xuan Yin): AI in healthcare relies on sensitive data like medical records and scans. Hackers may steal the patients' data, resulting in a data breach. Even if personal details are removed, people may still be identified through re-identification.

    (Professor): If you use a generative AI tool, the AI service provider would need that data to train the system, so there is a risk of data breach there. Separately, if patient information becomes part of training data, the AI system may inadvertently disclose patient data just by its functioning.

    (Low Xuan Yin)：医疗领域的人工智能依赖于敏感数据，如病历和扫描图。黑客可能会窃取患者数据，导致数据泄露。即使删除了个人详细信息，人们仍可能通过重新识别（re-identification）被认出。

    (教授)：如果你使用生成式人工智能工具，人工智能服务提供商需要这些数据来训练系统，因此存在数据泄露的风险。另外，如果患者信息成为训练数据的一部分，人工智能系统可能会在运作过程中无意泄露患者数据。

  - [20:22:21 - 20:23:54] **Risks: Lack of Empathy and Patient Centricity**

    (Pang Qin Wei): I think it's the ability to convey information with empathy. If you rely on AI to convey bad news, it's too cold—a "lifeless AI." A person mitigates the impact and comforts the family members more.

    (Professor): This forms part of the notion of patient centricity. Doctors are supposed to focus on the patient as a human being, not just a disease to be cured. Part of that is understanding where the patient is coming from and communicating in a way that helps them address negative emotions. That is a big part of what being a doctor is about.

    (Pang Qin Wei)：我认为是带着同理心传达信息的能力。如果你依靠人工智能来传达坏消息，那太冷漠了——一个“没有生命的AI”。人可以减轻影响，更多地安慰家属。

    (教授)：这构成了“以患者为中心”理念的一部分。医生应该关注作为一个人的患者，而不仅仅是需要治愈的疾病。这其中的一部分是理解患者的处境，并以一种帮助他们应对负面情绪的方式进行沟通。这是做医生的重要组成部分。

  - [20:23:54 - 20:27:06] **Accountability and Chat Comments**

    (Liang Kaixin): When it comes to life and death, it will be difficult for AI to recommend diagnosis when there is not much accountability.

    (Professor): Accountability is always a concern. If a hospital relies on AI to recommend treatments that are potentially life and death, and the recommendation is wrong, who should be held accountable? The hospital, the clinician, or the AI service provider?

    I see some comments in the chat. Tomo mentioned privacy and security threats. Christine expanded on over-dependence: certain medical decisions (like resuscitation) must be made urgently. You cannot have practitioners turn to an AI system in an emergency; you need them to act on the spot. Tomo also mentioned the impact on patient trust. Most of us would prefer a human doctor because of the human connection. If you don't trust your medical practitioner, you are not going to follow what they say.

    (Liang Kaixin)：当涉及到生死时，如果没有足够的问责制，人工智能很难推荐诊断。

    (教授)：问责制始终是一个问题。如果医院依靠人工智能推荐可能关乎生死的治疗方案，而推荐是错误的，谁应该负责？医院、临床医生还是人工智能服务提供商？

    我看到聊天里的一些评论。Tomo 提到了隐私和安全威胁。Christine 扩展了过度依赖的观点：某些医疗决定（如复苏）必须紧急做出。在紧急情况下，你不能让从业者求助于人工智能系统；你需要他们当场采取行动。Tomo 还提到了对患者信任的影响。我们大多数人更喜欢人类医生，因为有人际连接。如果你不信任你的医生，你就不会遵从他们的医嘱。

  - [20:27:06 - 20:30:49] **Brain-Computer Interfaces**

    (Tan Tit Ho): I wanted to discuss a scenario: brain-computer interfaces (BCI), like Elon Musk's Neuralink. It helps people with motor neuron diseases control devices. But there is talk about enhancing normal people to be superhuman—imagine a ChatGPT in your brain. A Bloomberg article discussed that if this is planted in everyone, big tech companies can harvest data directly from your brain—reading your intentions and preferences to manipulate your mind to purchase goods. So a medically provided AI tool could become a manipulation tool.

    (Professor): You are talking about a specific use case of AI for a medical device. The ethical concerns relate to whether we should allow for the use of this particular neuro-medical device. Should you allow companies to plant these devices in people's heads? There is a *Black Mirror* episode that addresses this theme. While these concerns are quite specific, this use case definitely raises an interesting set of ethical concerns.

    (Tan Tit Ho)：我想讨论一个场景：脑机接口（BCI），像埃隆·马斯克的 Neuralink。它帮助患有运动神经元疾病的人控制设备。但也有谈论说要增强普通人，使其成为超人——想象一下你大脑里有个 ChatGPT。一篇彭博社的文章讨论说，如果每个人都植入这个，大型科技公司可以直接从你的大脑中收割数据——读取你的意图和偏好，操纵你的思想去购买商品。因此，医疗提供的人工智能工具可能会变成操纵工具。

    (教授)：你在谈论人工智能作为医疗设备的特定用例。这里的伦理问题涉及我们是否应该允许使用这种特定的神经医疗设备。你应该允许公司把这些设备植入人们的脑袋吗？有一集《黑镜》专门探讨了这个主题。虽然这些担忧相当具体，但这个用例绝对引发了一系列有趣的伦理问题。

  - [20:30:49 - 20:34:47] **Conclusion: Two-Tier System**

    In the chat, Mithani mentioned that humans require empathy even for small illnesses. Ghazali mentioned medical AI may lack transparency, which prevents patients from having peace of mind about what is happening to them. Amanda mentioned the loss of core humanistic values like compassion and trustworthiness.

    If there are no other comments, I should raise one last thing to consider: the risk of the formation of a "two-tier system." One possible future we may see—for both legal and medical services—is where those who can afford it get access to human doctors and surgeons, while those who cannot afford it have to rely on machines. This gives rise to the question: is this type of inequality consistent with a just society? Even if it promotes access to medicine, is this the way we want to do it?

    I think most of the important points have been raised. That's all we have for today's lesson. I will upload the reading list for next week very soon. I will see you all next week when we go back to in-person lessons.

    聊天中，Mithani 提到即使是小病，人类也需要同理心。Ghazali 提到医疗人工智能可能缺乏透明度，这让患者无法对自己身上发生的事情感到安心。Amanda 提到了同情心和诚信等核心人文价值观的丧失。

    如果没有其他评论，我要提出最后一点供大家思考：“双轨制”（two-tier system）形成的风险。我们在法律和医疗服务中可能看到的一种未来是：那些负担得起的人可以看人类医生和外科医生，而那些负担不起的人只能依赖机器。这就引发了一个问题：这种不平等是否符合一个公正的社会？即使它促进了医疗服务的普及，这是我们要的方式吗？

    我想大部分重要观点都已经提到了。这就是今天课程的全部内容。我很快会上传下周的阅读书单。下周恢复线下课程时见。
***

# Reading
## Week 1
  - Introduction to AI
    - Adriana Placani, ‘Anthropomorphism in AI: hype and fallacy’ (2024) 4 AI and Ethics 691.
    - Alva Markelius and others, ‘The mechanisms of AI hype and its planetary and social costs’ (2024) 4 AI and Ethics 727.
    - Blake Richards and others, ‘The Illusion of AI’s Existential Risk’ (Noema, 2023).
  - Introduction to AI ethics
    - Sheila Bonde and Paul Firenze, ‘A Framework for Making Ethical Decisions’ (2013).
    - (OPTIONAL) Frank Aragbonfoh Abumere, ‘Utilitarianism’ in George Matthews (ed), Introduction to Philosophy: Ethics (2019).
    - (OPTIONAL) Joseph Kranak, ‘Kantian Deontology’ in George Matthews (ed), Introduction to Philosophy: Ethics (2019).
    - (OPTIONAL) Douglas Giles, ‘How Can I Be a Better Person? On Virtue Ethics’ in George Matthews (ed), Introduction to Philosophy: Ethics (2019).
  - Introduction to AI governance
    - Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development, ‘Recommendation of the Council on Artificial Intelligence’ (2025), section 1.
    - Association of Southeast Asian Nations, ‘ASEAN Guide on AI Governance and Ethics’ (2024) at pages 10-16.
    - Marco Pasqua, ‘Bridging Soft and Hard Law in AI Governance’ (2025).
## Week 2
  - Ethics – autonomous weapons
    - Peter Asaro, ‘Autonomous Weapons and the Ethics of Artificial Intelligence’ in S Matthew Liao (ed), Ethics of Artificial Intelligence (Oxford University Press 2020).
    - Michael Haiden and Florian Richter, ‘Autonomous weapons: considering the rights and interests of soldiers’ (2025) 27 Ethics and Information Technology 52.
  - Ethics – autonomous vehicles
    - Sven Ove Hansson, Matts-Åke Belin and Björn Lundgren, ‘Self-Driving Vehicles – an Ethical Overview’ (2021) 34 Philosophy and Technology 1383.
    - Alexander Hevelke and Julian Nida-Rümelin, ‘Responsibility for Crashes of Autonomous Vehicles: An Ethical Analysis’ (2015) 21 Science and Engineering Ethics 619.
    - Antje von Ungern-Sternberg, ‘Autonomous driving: regulatory challenges raised by artificial decision-making and tragic choices’ in Woodrow Barfield and Ugo Pagallo (eds), Research Handbook on the Law of Artificial Intelligence (Elgar 2018).
## Week 3
  - **Ethics – AI-facilitated anti-competitive business practices.** What does it mean for a business practice to be anti-competitive? What anti- competitive business practices does AI facilitate, and how does AI facilitate those practices? Why are such anti-competitive business practices unethical?
    - Maurice E Stucke and Ariel Ezrachi, ‘Antitrust, algorithmic pricing and tacit collusion’ in Woodrow Barfield and Ugo Pagallo (eds), Research Handbook on the Law of Artificial Intelligence (Elgar 2018).
    - Thomas K Cheng and Julian Nowag, ‘Algorithmic Predation and Exclusion’ (2023) 25 University of Pennsylvania Journal of Business Law 41.
  - **Ethics – AI-facilitated personalised pricing.** What is personalised pricing? How does AI facilitate personalised pricing? Why might personalised pricing be unethical (and is it always so)?
    - Akiva A Miller, ‘What Do We Worry About When We Worry About Price Discrimination? The Law and Ethics of Using Personal Information for Pricing’ (2014) 19 Journal of Technology Law and Policy 41.
    - Jeffery Moriarty, ‘Why online personalized pricing is unfair’ (2021) 23 Ethics and Information Technology 495.
## Week 4
  - **Ethics – Deepfakes** What are the harms of deepfakes, and are the ethical issues with deepfakes principally about their potentially harmful consequences? Might the making of deepfakes be intrinsically wrongful?
    - Adrienne de Ruiter, ‘The Distinct Wrong of Deepfakes’ (2021) 34 Philosophy & Technology 1311.
    - Daniel Story and Ryan Jenkins, ‘Deepfake Pornography and the Ethics of Non‑Veridical Representations’ (2023) 36 Philosophy & Technology 55.
    - Bobby Chesney and Danielle Citron, ‘Deep Fakes: A Looming Challenge for Privacy, Democracy, and National Security’ (2019) California Law Review 1753.
  - **Ethics – Facial recognition** What might be the ethical problems with the use of facial recognition technology? Does it matter (i) who is using it, (ii) where it is used, (iii) and why it is used? What are the social implications if the use of facial recognition technology is widespread?
    - Philip Brey, ‘Ethical Aspects of Facial Recognition Systems in Public Places’ (2004) 2 Journal of Information, Communication and Ethics in Society 97.
    - Evan Selinger and Brenda Leong, ‘The Ethics of Facial Recognition Technology’ in Carissa Véliz (ed), The Oxford Handbook of Digital Ethics (Oxford University Press 2024).
## Week 5
  - **Ethics – legal automation** What are the risks of using AI in predictive policing? Should AI replace judges in court? What are the potential ethical problems with relying on AI to provide legal advice?
    - Andrew Guthrie Ferguson, ‘Policing Predictive Policing’ (2017) 94 Washington University Law Review 1109.
    - Tania Sourdin, ‘Judge v Robot? Artificial Intelligence and Judicial Decision- Making’ (2018) 41 UNSW Law Journal 1114.
    - Xin Dai, ‘Who Wants a Robo-Lawyer Now?: On AI Chatbots in China’s Public Legal Services Sector’ (2024) 26 Yale Journal of Law & Technology 527.
  - **Ethics – medical automation** What risks arise when AI is used for the provision of medical services? Would it be ethical to substitute a clinician with an AI tool?
    - Jens Christian Bjerring and Jacob Busch, ‘Artificial Intelligence and Patient- Centered Decision-Making’ (2021) 34 Philosophy & Technology 349.
    - Amitabha Palmer and David Schwan, ‘Advanced Technologies in Medicine: Safeguarding Physician Skill, Knowledge, and Character in the AI-Enhanced Clinic in Matthew C Altman and David Schwan (eds), Ethics and Medical Technology: Essays on Artificial Intelligence, Enhancement, Privacy, and Justice (Springer 2025).
## Week 6
  - **Ethics – human-AI relationships** What are the personal ethical implications of the formation of human-AI relationships? Are there moral problems with creating companion AI, or allowing AI to be used in such a way?
    - Emilia Kaczmarek, ‘Self-Deception in Human-AI Emotional Relations’ (2025) 42 Journal of Applied Philosophy 814.
    - Kim Malfacini, ‘The impacts of companion AI on human relationships: risks, benefits, and design considerations’ (2025) 40 AI & Society 5527.
  - **Ethics – broader social implications** What are some ethical concerns with the use of AI for “social” scoring? How might AI shape the future of work, and what ethical implications do these shapings have?
    - Danielle Keats Citron and Frank Pasquale, ‘The Scored Society: Due Process for Automated Predictions’ (2014) 89 Washington Law Review 1.
    - John Danaher, ‘Automation and the Future of Work’ in Carissa Véliz (ed), The Oxford Handbook of Digital Ethics (Oxford University Press 2024).
***
